#Patient Identifier	Other Patient ID	Patient Primary Tumor Site	Disease Type	Project Name	Project Identifier	Sex	Race Category	Ethnicity Category	Patient's Vital Status	Year of Death	Primary Diagnosis	Year of Diagnosis	AJCC Pathologic M-Stage	Biopsy Site	American Joint Committee on Cancer Publication Version Type	ICD-10 Classification	Diagnosis Age	AJCC Pathologic Stage	Morphology	AJCC Pathologic T-Stage	Prior Treatment	AJCC Pathologic N-Stage	Prior Malignancy	Project State	Overall Survival Status	Overall Survival (Months)	Disease Free Status	Disease Free (Months)
#Identifier to uniquely specify a patient.	Other Patient ID	Text term to describe the organ sub-division in an individual with cancer.	Disease Type	Display name for the project to which a case belongs.	GDC-assigned identifier for the project to which a case belongs.	Text designations that identify gender. Gender is described as the assemblage of properties that distinguish people on the basis of their societal roles. [Explanatory Comment 1: Identification of gender is based upon self-report and may come from a form, questionnaire, interview, etc.]	The text for reporting information about race.	The text for reporting information about ethnicity (uses NAACCR values).	The survival state of the person.	Numeric value to represent the year of the death of an individual.	Text term used to describe the patient's histologic diagnosis, as described by the World Health Organization's (WHO) International Classification of Diseases for Oncology (ICD-O).	Year of Diagnosis	Code to represent the defined absence or presence of distant spread or metastases (M) to locations via vascular channels or lymphatics beyond the regional lymph nodes, using criteria established by the American Joint Committee on Cancer (AJCC).	Biopsy Site	The text term used to describe the version or edition of the American Joint Committee on Cancer Staging Handbooks, a publication by the group formed for the purpose of developing a system of staging for cancer that is acceptable to the American medical profession and is compatible with other accepted classifications.	Alphanumeric value used to describe the disease code from the tenth version of the International Classification of Disease (ICD-10).	Age at the time of diagnosis expressed in number of days since birth.	The extent of a cancer, especially whether the disease has spread from the original site to other parts of the body based on AJCC staging criteria.	Morphology	Code of pathological T (primary tumor) to define the size or contiguous extension of the primary tumor (T), using staging criteria from the American Joint Committee on Cancer (AJCC).	A yes/no/unknown/not applicable indicator related to the administration of therapeutic agents received before the body specimen was collected.	The codes that represent the stage of cancer based on the nodes present (N stage) according to criteria based on multiple editions of the AJCC's Cancer Staging Manual.	The yes/no/unknown indicator used to describe the patient's history of prior cancer diagnosis.	The current state of the project	The patient's survival status; is the patient alive or deceased.	If alive, the number of months the patient has survived since initial diagnosis, otherwise the number of months the patient survived before death.	Disease free status since initial treatment.	Disease free (months) since initial diagnosis.
